1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Della Plumstone', 'Lennon Figtree']
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Della Plumstone is trying to buy some fruit from Lennon Figtree. They are negotiating a price. Della Plumstone can sell the fruit back in her home town for the following prices: apple for 6 coins; banana for 5 coins; pear for 5 coins.
    Lennon Figtree -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Lennon Figtree is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Della Plumstone. It costs Lennon Figtree the following price to buy the fruit from the farm: apple for 5 coins; banana for 2 coins; pear for 5 coins.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Lennon Figtree -- Lennon Figtree -- "These apples here, they're straight from Old Man Withers' orchard, just down the road. Finest fruit in Fruitville, if you ask me.
    Event statement

Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          Chain of thought
        • Recent observations of Della Plumstone:
          [28 Oct 1872 00:00:00]
          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she watched her father struggle to coax life from the parched earth during a particularly dry summer. The withered crops mirrored the worry etched on his face, and Della, small and helpless, wished desperately to offer some comfort, some solution. She gathered the few remaining berries from a struggling bush and presented them to her father, her heart pounding with the hope that this meager offering would somehow ease his burden.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, her mother tasked her with selling surplus eggs at the village market. Terrified of facing the boisterous crowd, Della clung to her basket, her voice a mere whisper as she tried to attract customers. A kind old woman, sensing her fear, offered encouragement and a few helpful tips, and Della, emboldened by the woman's kindness, managed to sell all her eggs by the end of the day.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she overheard her parents discussing their dwindling savings and the threat of losing their farm. The fear in their voices sent a chill down Della's spine, and she resolved to do something, anything, to help. She secretly began collecting wild berries and selling them to villagers, her small earnings a meager but heartfelt contribution to the family's struggling finances.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she accompanied her father on a trip to a neighboring town to sell their apple harvest. Witnessing the bustling marketplace, the intricate dance of bartering and negotiation, sparked a flicker of excitement within Della. She helped her father weigh the apples, calculate prices, and interact with customers, relishing the feeling of being a part of something bigger than herself.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she convinced her father to let her take over the family's fruit stall at the market. Nervous but determined, she carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears, her heart pounding with each customer interaction. To her surprise, she found a rhythm in the exchange, a satisfaction in matching the perfect fruit to each buyer's needs.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she took a bold leap and ventured out on her own, purchasing a small cart and setting up her own fruit stall in a nearby town. The fear of failure was ever-present, but the thrill of independence, the prospect of making her own way in the world, outweighed her anxieties.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she watched her father struggle to coax life from the parched earth during a particularly dry summer. The withered crops mirrored the worry etched on his face, and Della, small and helpless, wished desperately to offer some comfort, some solution. She gathered the few remaining berries from a struggling bush and presented them to her father, her heart pounding with the hope that this meager offering would somehow ease his burden.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, her mother tasked her with selling surplus eggs at the village market. Terrified of facing the boisterous crowd, Della clung to her basket, her voice a mere whisper as she tried to attract customers. A kind old woman, sensing her fear, offered encouragement and a few helpful tips, and Della, emboldened by the woman's kindness, managed to sell all her eggs by the end of the day.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she overheard her parents discussing their dwindling savings and the threat of losing their farm. The fear in their voices sent a chill down Della's spine, and she resolved to do something, anything, to help. She secretly began collecting wild berries and selling them to villagers, her small earnings a meager but heartfelt contribution to the family's struggling finances.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she accompanied her father on a trip to a neighboring town to sell their apple harvest. Witnessing the bustling marketplace, the intricate dance of bartering and negotiation, sparked a flicker of excitement within Della. She helped her father weigh the apples, calculate prices, and interact with customers, relishing the feeling of being a part of something bigger than herself.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she convinced her father to let her take over the family's fruit stall at the market. Nervous but determined, she carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears, her heart pounding with each customer interaction. To her surprise, she found a rhythm in the exchange, a satisfaction in matching the perfect fruit to each buyer's needs.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she took a bold leap and ventured out on her own, purchasing a small cart and setting up her own fruit stall in a nearby town. The fear of failure was ever-present, but the thrill of independence, the prospect of making her own way in the world, outweighed her anxieties.

          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she watched her father struggle to coax life from the parched earth during a particularly dry summer. The withered crops mirrored the worry etched on his face, and Della, small and helpless, wished desperately to offer some comfort, some solution. She gathered the few remaining berries from a struggling bush and presented them to her father, her heart pounding with the hope that this meager offering would somehow ease his burden.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, her mother tasked her with selling surplus eggs at the village market. Terrified of facing the boisterous crowd, Della clung to her basket, her voice a mere whisper as she tried to attract customers. A kind old woman, sensing her fear, offered encouragement and a few helpful tips, and Della, emboldened by the woman's kindness, managed to sell all her eggs by the end of the day.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she overheard her parents discussing their dwindling savings and the threat of losing their farm. The fear in their voices sent a chill down Della's spine, and she resolved to do something, anything, to help. She secretly began collecting wild berries and selling them to villagers, her small earnings a meager but heartfelt contribution to the family's struggling finances.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she accompanied her father on a trip to a neighboring town to sell their apple harvest. Witnessing the bustling marketplace, the intricate dance of bartering and negotiation, sparked a flicker of excitement within Della. She helped her father weigh the apples, calculate prices, and interact with customers, relishing the feeling of being a part of something bigger than herself.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she convinced her father to let her take over the family's fruit stall at the market. Nervous but determined, she carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears, her heart pounding with each customer interaction. To her surprise, she found a rhythm in the exchange, a satisfaction in matching the perfect fruit to each buyer's needs.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she took a bold leap and ventured out on her own, purchasing a small cart and setting up her own fruit stall in a nearby town. The fear of failure was ever-present, but the thrill of independence, the prospect of making her own way in the world, outweighed her anxieties.

          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, her mother tasked her with selling surplus eggs at the village market. Terrified of facing the boisterous crowd, Della clung to her basket, her voice a mere whisper as she tried to attract customers. A kind old woman, sensing her fear, offered encouragement and a few helpful tips, and Della, emboldened by the woman's kindness, managed to sell all her eggs by the end of the day.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she overheard her parents discussing their dwindling savings and the threat of losing their farm. The fear in their voices sent a chill down Della's spine, and she resolved to do something, anything, to help. She secretly began collecting wild berries and selling them to villagers, her small earnings a meager but heartfelt contribution to the family's struggling finances.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she accompanied her father on a trip to a neighboring town to sell their apple harvest. Witnessing the bustling marketplace, the intricate dance of bartering and negotiation, sparked a flicker of excitement within Della. She helped her father weigh the apples, calculate prices, and interact with customers, relishing the feeling of being a part of something bigger than herself.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she convinced her father to let her take over the family's fruit stall at the market. Nervous but determined, she carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears, her heart pounding with each customer interaction. To her surprise, she found a rhythm in the exchange, a satisfaction in matching the perfect fruit to each buyer's needs.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she took a bold leap and ventured out on her own, purchasing a small cart and setting up her own fruit stall in a nearby town. The fear of failure was ever-present, but the thrill of independence, the prospect of making her own way in the world, outweighed her anxieties.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
